        <meta property="og:url" content="https://pubs.acs.org/doi/full/10.1021/acsami.0c11616"><meta property="og:title" content="Iron-Doped Sodium Vanadium Oxyflurophosphate Cathodes for Sodium-Ion Batteries—Electrochemical Characterization and In Situ Measurements of Heat Generation"><meta property="og:image" content="https://pubs.acs.org/cms/10.1021/acsami.0c11616/asset/images/acsami.0c11616.social.jpeg_v03"><meta property="og:description" content="Sodium-ion batteries (NaIBs) are increasingly being envisioned for grid-scale energy-storage systems because of cost advantages. However, implementation of this vision has been challenged by the low-energy densities delivered by most NaIB cathodes. Toward addressing this challenge, the authors report the synthesis and characterization of a new iron-doped Na3Fe0.3V1.7O(PO4)2F2 cathode using a novel facile hydrothermal route. The synthesized material was characterized using scanning electron microscopy, X-ray diffraction, and Mössbauer spectroscopy techniques. The obtained discharge capacity in the half-cell configuration lies from 119 to 125 to 130 mA h/g at C/10 while tested using three different electrolyte formulations, dimethyl carbonate–ethylene carbonate (EC)–propylene carbonate (PC), diethyl carbonate–EC, and EC–PC, respectively. The synthesized cathodes were also evaluated in full-cell configurations, which delivered an initial discharge capacity of 80 mA h/g with NaTi2(PO4)3MWCNT as the anode. Ionic diffusivity and interfacial charge transfer kinetics were also evaluated as a function of temperature and sodium concentration, which revealed that electrochemical rate performances in this material were limited by charge-transfer kinetics. To understand the heat generation mechanism of the Na/Na3Fe0.3V1.7O(PO4)2F2 half-cell during charge and discharge processes, an electrochemical isothermal calorimetry measurement was carried out at different current rates for two different temperatures (25 and 45 °C). The results showed that the amount of heat generated was strongly affected by the operating charge/discharge state, C-rate, and temperature. Overall, this work provides a new synthesis route for the development of iron-doped Na3Fe0.3V1.7O(PO4)2F2-based high-performance sodium cathode materials aimed at providing a viable pathway for the development and deployment of large-scale energy-storage based on sodium battery systems."><meta property="og:type" content="Article"><meta property="og:site_name" content="ACS Publications"><meta name="twitter:card" content="summary_large_image"><meta name="twitter:site" content="@ACSPublications"><meta name="twitter:image" content="https://pubs.acs.org/cms/10.1021/acsami.0c11616/asset/images/acsami.0c11616.social.jpeg_v03">

<!-- loading Javascript for using the persistence Service -->
    <script src="/wro/nwyw~thiss-ds.js" async="" nonce="90f6e33bfd1a775c-LHR"></script>

    <script type="text/javascript" nonce="90f6e33bfd1a775c-LHR">

        var SeamlessAccessService = {
            spUrl: "/action/ssostart",
            returnURL: window.location.href,
            my_context: 'seamlessaccess.org',
            timeout: 5000,

            getWAYFLessUrl: function (entityId) {
                return this.spUrl + "?idp=" + encodeURIComponent(entityId)
                    + "&redirectUri=" + encodeURIComponent(this.returnURL);
            },
            retrieveEntity: function (ms) {
                var self = this;
                var persistService = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                if (ms == undefined || ms === '') {
                    ms = this.timeout;
                }

                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    persistService.entities(self.my_context)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            return resolve(res.data);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            reject('failed to retrieve entity from local storage: ' + err);
                        });
                    // Set up the timeout
                    setTimeout(function () {
                        reject('Promise timed out ' + ms + ' ms');
                    }, ms);
                });
            },
            updateEntity: function (entitydata) {
                var self = this;
                var persistService = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                var jsonObj = {};
                try {
                    //try to parse it, if it is a json string
                    jsonObj = JSON.parse(entitydata.val());
                } catch (e) {
                    jsonObj = entitydata;
                }
                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    persistService.update(self.my_context, jsonObj)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            // Process the results
                            var ssoInstitutions = res.data;
                            return resolve(ssoInstitutions);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            console.log('failed to update the local storage due to: ' + err);
                            reject(err);
                        });
                })
            },
            removeEntity: function (entityId) {
                var self = this;
                var persistService = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                return new Promise(function (resolve) {
                    persistService.remove(self.my_context, entityId)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            return resolve(res);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            console.log('failed to remove from local storage duo to: ' + err);
                        });
                })
            },
            getAccessibleEntityStatus: function (doi, entityId, entityTitle) {
                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    $.ajax({
                        type: 'POST',
                        url: '/action/seamlessAccess',
                        accept: {
                            text: "application/json"
                        },
                        data: {
                            doi: doi,
                            entityid: entityId,
                            entityTitle: entityTitle,
                            eventGroupKey: '73daf7b7-2fc1-44c9-9b80-9f491086b5d6'
                        }

                    }).done(function (status) {
                        return resolve(status);
                    }).fail(function (status) {
                        return reject(status);
                    });
                });
            },
            getEntitiesWithAllInfo: function (doi) {
                let self = this,
                    arrayOfPromises = [];
                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    self.retrieveEntity().then(function (res) {
                        let allSsoInstitutions = res;
                        for (i = 0; i < allSsoInstitutions.length; i++) {
                            let ssoInstitution = allSsoInstitutions[i];
                            arrayOfPromises.push(new Promise(function (resolve) {
                                self.getAccessibleEntityStatus(doi, ssoInstitution.entity.entityID, ssoInstitution.entity.title)
                                    .then(function (entityStatus) {
                                        resolve({
                                            entityID: ssoInstitution.entity.entityID,
                                            entityTitle: ssoInstitution.entity.title,
                                            entityStatusObj: entityStatus,
                                            entitySsoUrl: self.getWAYFLessUrl(ssoInstitution.entity.entityID)
                                        });
                                    }, function (err) {
                                        console.log('failed to get the entity status: ' + ssoInstitution.entity.entityID,err);
                                    });
                            }));
                        }
                        if(allSsoInstitutions.length === 0 && true){
                            self.getAccessibleEntityStatus(doi, null, null)
                                .then(function () {
                                    console.log('No Entity found');
                                }, function (err) {
                                    console.log('failed to get the none entity status' ,err);
                                });
                        }
                        Promise.all(arrayOfPromises)
                            .then(function (finalResponse) {
                                resolve(finalResponse);
                            }).catch(function (err) {
                                reject(err);
                            });

                    }).catch(function (err) {
                        reject(err);
                    })
                });
            }
        };

        window.addEventListener('load', function () {
            document.querySelectorAll(".sso-institution").forEach(function (institution) {
                var entityId = institution.getAttribute('data-entityid');
                var entityName = institution.getAttribute('data-name');
                var entitydata = {
                    entityID: entityId,
                    title: entityName
                };
                institution.addEventListener("click", function (e) {
                    e.preventDefault();

                    if ($('.institution-preference-userconsent-checkbox').length > 0) {
                        let institutionPreferenceUserConsentCheckbox = $('.institution-preference-userconsent-checkbox').get(0);
                        if (!$(institutionPreferenceUserConsentCheckbox).is(":checked")) {
                            return;
                        }
                    }

                    var self = this;
                    SeamlessAccessService.updateEntity(entitydata).then(function (res) {
                        console.log(res);
                        window.location.href = self.href;
                    }).catch(function (err) {
                        window.location.href = self.href;
                    });
                });
            });
        });

    </script>

<script type="text/javascript" nonce="90f6e33bfd1a775c-LHR">
var dfpReady = false;
$(document).ready(function() {
    // var journalTitle = 'applied_materials_interfaces';
    var taxonomyKeywords = $('.article_header-taxonomy');
    var articleKeyword = $('meta[name="keywords"]');
    var articleTitle = $('meta[name="dc.Title"]');
    var articleDescription = $('meta[name="dc.Description"]');
    var abstractKeyword = $('p.articleBody_abstractText:contains("Keywords: ")');
    var searchTerms = [];

    if (taxonomyKeywords.length > 0) {
        $(taxonomyKeywords).children(".rlist--inline").children("li").each(function() {
            searchTerms.push($(this).text());
        });
    }
    else if (articleKeyword.length > 0) { 
        searchTerms = searchTerms.concat(articleKeyword.prop('content').split(', '));
    }
    else if (abstractKeyword.length > 0) {
        searchTerms = searchTerms.concat(abstractKeyword.text().split("Keywords: ")[1].split('; '));
    }
    else if (articleDescription.length > 0) {
        $(articleDescription).each(function() {
            articleDescriptionKeywords = $(this).prop('content');
            articleDescriptionKeywords = articleDescriptionKeywords.replace(/.,/g,"");
            articleDescriptionKeywords = articleDescriptionKeywords.replace(/\s{2,}/g," ");
            searchTerms = searchTerms.concat(articleDescriptionKeywords.split(' '));
        });
    }

    if (articleTitle.length > 0) {
        searchTerms = searchTerms.concat(articleTitle.prop('content').split(' '));
    }

    googletag.cmd.push(function() {
        var mappingLeader = googletag.sizeMapping().
        addSize([750, 200], [728, 90]). 
        addSize([0, 0], [320, 50]).
        build();
        //leaderboard
        googletag.defineSlot('/8868/journal/applied_materials_interfaces/article', [728, 90], 'dfp-journal-article-leaderboard').defineSizeMapping(mappingLeader).setTargeting('location', 'leaderboard1').setTargeting('Keyword', searchTerms).addService(googletag.pubads());
        //recommend
        googletag.defineSlot("/8868/journal/applied_materials_interfaces/article", [1, 1], "dfp-journal-article-recommend").setTargeting("ntvPlacement", ["1100167"]).setTargeting("location", "recommend").setTargeting('Keyword', searchTerms).addService(googletag.pubads());
        //googletag.pubads().enableSingleRequest();
        googletag.pubads().collapseEmptyDivs();
        googletag.pubads().setTargeting('inst',dartInstitutionType).setTargeting('memb',dartMember);
        googletag.pubads().addEventListener("slotRenderEnded", function(event) {
            console.log(event.slot.getSlotElementId() + " isEmpty: " + event.isEmpty + " | creative id: " + event.creativeId + " " + event.size[0] + "x" + event.size[1]);
            if((event.isEmpty === false) && (event.slot.getSlotElementId() != "dfp-journal-article-recommend")) {
                $("#" + event.slot.getSlotElementId()).parents(".advertisement").slideDown();
                console.log("ad display: " + event.creativeId + " " + event.size[0] + "x" + event.size[1]);
            }
            // else {
            //     console.log("no ad found");
            // }
        });
        googletag.enableServices();
        dfpReady = true;
    });
});
</script>

    var serialCode = "aamick";
    var books = ["reagents", "symposium", "advances", "medichemreviews", "styleguide"]
    if(books.includes(serialCode) === false) {
        // default click action
        $("[data-id]").on("mousedown", function(e) {
            var currentClickID = $(this).attr("data-id");

            if(currentClickID.includes("_hover") === false) {
                if(currentClickID.match("^article_") && !currentClickID.match("^article_abstract_CC")) {   
                    gtag('event', "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Iron-Doped Sodium Vanadium Oxyflurophosphate Cathodes for Sodium-Ion Batteries—Electrochemical Characterization and In Situ Measurements of Heat Generation", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.0c11616", "Article_Element": $(this).attr("data-id") });
                }
            }
        });
        
        // Access Management icons hover
        var articleAccessManagementIconHover = false;
        var articleAccessManagementIconHoverEvent = false;
        $("[data-id='article_access_icon']").on("mouseenter", function(e) {
            if(articleAccessManagementIconHoverEvent === false) {
                articleAccessManagementIconHover = true;
                var articleAccessManagementHover =  $(this).attr("data-id") + "_hover";
                
                setTimeout(function() { 
                    if(articleAccessManagementIconHover === true) {
                        gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Iron-Doped Sodium Vanadium Oxyflurophosphate Cathodes for Sodium-Ion Batteries—Electrochemical Characterization and In Situ Measurements of Heat Generation", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.0c11616", "Article_Element": articleAccessManagementHover });
    
                        articleAccessManagementIconHoverEvent = true;
                    }
                }, 1000);
            }
        });
        $("[data-id='article_access_icon']").on("mouseleave", function(e) {
            articleAccessManagementIconHover = false;
        });
    
        // articleRightsPermissionsLink hover
        var articleRightsPermissionsLinkHover = false;
        var articleRightsPermissionsLinkHoverEvent = false;
        $("[data-id='article_rights_permissions']").on("mouseenter", function(e) {
            if(articleRightsPermissionsLinkHoverEvent === false) {
                articleRightsPermissionsLinkHover = true;
                var articleRightsHover =  $(this).attr("data-id") + "_hover";
                
                setTimeout(function() { 
                    if(articleRightsPermissionsLinkHover === true) {
                        gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Iron-Doped Sodium Vanadium Oxyflurophosphate Cathodes for Sodium-Ion Batteries—Electrochemical Characterization and In Situ Measurements of Heat Generation", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.0c11616", "Article_Element": articleRightsHover });
    
                        articleRightsPermissionsLinkHoverEvent = true;
                    }
                }, 1000);
            }
        });
        $("[data-id='article_rights_permissions']").on("mouseleave", function(e) {
            articleRightsPermissionsLinkHover = false;
        });
    
        // Author hover
        var articleAuthorHover = false
        var articleAuthorHoverEvent = false
        $("[data-id='article_author_info']").on("mouseenter", function(e) {
            if((articleAuthorHoverEvent === false) && ($(this).parent().hasClass("view-affs") === false)) {
                articleAuthorHover = true;
                var authorInfoHover =  $(this).attr("data-id") + "_hover";
                
                setTimeout(function() { 
                    if((articleAuthorHover === true) && (articleAuthorHoverEvent === false)) {
                        gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Iron-Doped Sodium Vanadium Oxyflurophosphate Cathodes for Sodium-Ion Batteries—Electrochemical Characterization and In Situ Measurements of Heat Generation", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.0c11616", "Article_Element": authorInfoHover });
    
                        articleAuthorHoverEvent = true;
                    }
                }, 1000);
            }
        });
        $("[data-id='article_author_info']").on("mouseleave", function(e) {
            articleAuthorHover = false;
        });
    
        // CC License hover
        var articleAbstractCCHover = false
        var articleAbstractCCHoverEvent = false
        var articleDrawerCCHover = false
        var articleDrawerCCHoverEvent = false
        $(".article__cc-license__inter a").on("mouseenter", function(e) {
            if($(this).attr("data-id")) {
                if(($(this).attr("data-id") === "article_drawer_CC-License") && (articleDrawerCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                    articleDrawerCCHover = true;
                    
                    setTimeout(function() { 
                        if((articleDrawerCCHover === true) && (articleDrawerCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                            gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Iron-Doped Sodium Vanadium Oxyflurophosphate Cathodes for Sodium-Ion Batteries—Electrochemical Characterization and In Situ Measurements of Heat Generation", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.0c11616", "Article_Element": "article_drawer_CC-License_hover" });
    
                            articleDrawerCCHoverEvent = true;
                        }
                    }, 1000);
                }
                else if(($(this).attr("data-id").match("^article_abstract_CC")) && (articleAbstractCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                    articleAbstractCCHover = true;
    
                    setTimeout(function() { 
                        if((articleAbstractCCHover === true) && (articleAbstractCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                            gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Iron-Doped Sodium Vanadium Oxyflurophosphate Cathodes for Sodium-Ion Batteries—Electrochemical Characterization and In Situ Measurements of Heat Generation", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.0c11616", "Article_Element": "article_abstract_CC_hover" });
    
                            articleAbstractCCHoverEvent = true;
                        }
                    }, 1000);
                }
            }
            else if(($(this).hasClass("article__cc-license__link")) && (articleAbstractCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                articleAbstractCCHover = true;
                
                setTimeout(function() { 
                    if((articleAbstractCCHover === true) && (articleAbstractCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                        gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Iron-Doped Sodium Vanadium Oxyflurophosphate Cathodes for Sodium-Ion Batteries—Electrochemical Characterization and In Situ Measurements of Heat Generation", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.0c11616", "Article_Element": "article_abstract_CC_hover" });
    
                        articleAbstractCCHoverEvent = true;
                    }
                }, 1000);
            }
        });
        $(".article__cc-license__inter a").on("mouseleave", function(e) {
            if(articleAbstractCCHover === true) {
                articleAbstractCCHover = false;
            }
            if(articleDrawerCCHover = true) {
                articleDrawerCCHover = false;
            }
        });
        
        // show recommeneded click delay
        var intervalCount = 0;
        var showRecommendedInterval = setInterval(function() {
            intervalCount += 100;
            if($(".show-recommended__wrapper .show-recommended").length > 0) {
                clearInterval(showRecommendedInterval);
                $("[data-id='article_drawer_RecommendedShowMore']").on("mousedown", function(e) {
                    gtag('event', "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Iron-Doped Sodium Vanadium Oxyflurophosphate Cathodes for Sodium-Ion Batteries—Electrochemical Characterization and In Situ Measurements of Heat Generation", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.0c11616", "Article_Element": $(this).attr("data-id") });
                });
                $("[data-id='article_drawer_RecommendedShowLess']").on("mousedown", function(e) {
                    gtag('event', "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Iron-Doped Sodium Vanadium Oxyflurophosphate Cathodes for Sodium-Ion Batteries—Electrochemical Characterization and In Situ Measurements of Heat Generation", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.0c11616", "Article_Element": $(this).attr("data-id") });
                });
            }
        }, 100);
    }
});
</script>

Muralidharan</a></span></div><div class="loa-info-orcid"><img height="20" width="27" src="/products/achs/releasedAssets/images/orchid-2856f829046fbda55b90e1582edf0e9a.png" alt="Orcid"><a href="http://orcid.org/0000-0001-6042-5295" title="Orcid link">http://orcid.org/0000-0001-6042-5295</a></div></div></div></span></li><li><span><span class="hlFld-ContribAuthor" tabindex="0" data-id="article_author_info" property="author">Ramesh Kumar Petla</span><div class="loa-info hlFld-Affiliation"><div class="loa-info--wrapper"><div class="loa-info-name">Ramesh Kumar Petla</div><div class="loa-info-affiliations"><div class="loa-info-affiliations-info">Qatar Environment and Energy Research Institute (QEERI), Hamad Bin Khalifa University, Qatar Foundation, 34110 Doha, Qatar</div></div><div class="loa-info-scifinder"><span>More by <a href="/action/doSearch?field1=Contrib&amp;text1=Ramesh+Kumar++Petla" data-id="article_author_search">Ramesh Kumar Petla</a></span></div><div class="loa-info-orcid"><img height="20" width="27" src="/products/achs/releasedAssets/images/orchid-2856f829046fbda55b90e1582edf0e9a.png" alt="Orcid"><a href="http://orcid.org/0000-0001-9456-3370" title="Orcid link">http://orcid.org/0000-0001-9456-3370</a></div></div></div></span></li><li><span><span class="hlFld-ContribAuthor" tabindex="0" data-id="article_author_info" property="author">H. href="/servlet/linkout?type=rightslink&amp;url=startPage%3D41765%26pageCount%3D11%26copyright%3DAmerican%2BChemical%2BSociety%26author%3DR.%2BEssehli%252C%2BK.%2BMaher%252C%2BR.%2BAmin%252C%2Bet%2Bal%26orderBeanReset%3Dtrue%26imprint%3DAmerican%2BChemical%2BSociety%26volumeNum%3D12%26issueNum%3D37%26contentID%3Dacsami.0c11616%26title%3DIron-Doped%2BSodium%2BVanadium%2BOxyflurophosphate%2BCathodes%2Bfor%2BSodium-Ion%2BBatteries%25E2%2580%2594Electrochemical%2BCharacterization%2Band%2BIn%2BSitu%2BMeasurements%2Bof%2BHeat%2BGeneration%26numPages%3D11%26pa%3D%26issn%3D1944-8244%26publisherName%3Dacs%26publication%3Daamick%26rpt%3Dn%26endPage%3D41775%26publicationDate%3DSeptember%2B2020" Empty dropzone --></div></div></div></div><div class="article_abstract"><div class="article_abstract-title" id="Abstract" tabindex="0"><h2>Abstract</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div><div class="article_abstract-content hlFld-Abstract" id="abstractBox" property="description"><figure id="_i1" data-index="0" class="article__inlineFigure article_abstract-img"><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img class="inline-fig internalNav" src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.0c11616/asset/images/medium/am0c11616_0011.gif" alt="" id="tgr1" property="image" style="width:405px; height:275px"></button><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsami.0c11616/asset/images/large/am0c11616_0011.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsami.0c11616&amp;id=_i1"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><p class="articleBody_abstractText">Sodium-ion batteries (NaIBs) are increasingly being envisioned for grid-scale energy-storage systems because of cost advantages. However, implementation of this vision has been challenged by the low-energy densities delivered by most NaIB cathodes. Toward addressing this challenge, the authors report the synthesis and characterization of a new iron-doped Na<sub>3</sub>Fe<sub>0.3</sub>V<sub>1.7</sub>O(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>2</sub>F<sub>2</sub> cathode using a novel facile hydrothermal route. The synthesized material was characterized using scanning electron microscopy, X-ray diffraction, and Mössbauer spectroscopy techniques. The obtained discharge capacity in the half-cell configuration lies from 119 to 125 to 130 mA h/g at C/10 while tested using three different electrolyte formulations, dimethyl carbonate–ethylene carbonate (EC)–propylene carbonate (PC), diethyl carbonate–EC, and EC–PC, respectively. The synthesized cathodes were also evaluated in full-cell configurations, which delivered an initial discharge capacity of 80 mA h/g with NaTi<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub>MWCNT as the anode. Ionic diffusivity and interfacial charge transfer kinetics were also evaluated as a function of temperature and sodium concentration, which revealed that electrochemical rate performances in this material were limited by charge-transfer kinetics. To understand the heat generation mechanism of the Na/Na<sub>3</sub>Fe<sub>0.3</sub>V<sub>1.7</sub>O(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>2</sub>F<sub>2</sub> half-cell during charge and discharge processes, an electrochemical isothermal calorimetry measurement was carried out at different current rates for two different temperatures (25 and 45 °C). The results showed that the amount of heat generated was strongly affected by the operating charge/discharge state, C-rate, and temperature. Overall, this work provides a new synthesis route for the development of iron-doped Na<sub>3</sub>Fe<sub>0.3</sub>V<sub>1.7</sub>O(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>2</sub>F<sub>2</sub>-based high-performance sodium cathode materials aimed at providing a viable pathway for the development and deployment of large-scale energy-storage based on sodium battery systems.</p></div><div class="article__cc-license"><div class="article__cc-license__body"><p class="article__cc-license__para">This publication is licensed under the terms of your
                            institutional subscription.
                            <a href="/servlet/linkout?type=rightslink&amp;url=startPage%3D41765%26pageCount%3D11%26copyright%3DAmerican%2BChemical%2BSociety%26author%3DR.%2BEssehli%252C%2BK.%2BMaher%252C%2BR.%2BAmin%252C%2Bet%2Bal%26orderBeanReset%3Dtrue%26imprint%3DAmerican%2BChemical%2BSociety%26volumeNum%3D12%26issueNum%3D37%26contentID%3Dacsami.0c11616%26title%3DIron-Doped%2BSodium%2BVanadium%2BOxyflurophosphate%2BCathodes%2Bfor%2BSodium-Ion%2BBatteries%25E2%2580%2594Electrochemical%2BCharacterization%2Band%2BIn%2BSitu%2BMeasurements%2Bof%2BHeat%2BGeneration%26numPages%3D11%26pa%3D%26issn%3D1944-8244%26publisherName%3Dacs%26publication%3Daamick%26rpt%3Dn%26endPage%3D41775%26publicationDate%3DSeptember%2B2020" class="link--bold">Request reuse permissions.</a></p></div></div><span class="hidden" property="publisher">ACS Publications</span><div class="article_header-article-copyright">Copyright © 2020 American Chemical Society</div><div class="article_header-footer-right"><div class="articleHeaderDropzone7" data-pb-dropzone="articleHeaderDropzone7"><div class="article__tags article__tags--subjects"><div class="article__tags__container"><header class="article__tags__header"><h3 class="article__tags__heading">Subjects</h3><div tabindex="0" class="article__tags__tooltip"><div aria-describedby="tooltip-subjects" class="article__tags__icon"><i class="icon-info-circle-outline"></i><span class="sr-only">what are subjects</span></div><p id="tooltip-subjects" role="tooltip" class="article__tags__diff">Article subjects are automatically applied from the ACS Subject Taxonomy and describe the scientific concepts and themes of the article.</p></div></header><ul class="article__tags__list"><li class="article__tags__item"><a href="/action/doSearch?ConceptID=290830&amp;ref=fulltext" title="Diffusion" title="Electrochemical cells" data-id="article_abstract_Subject_Electrochemical%20cells" class="article__tags__link">Electrochemical cells</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"><a href="/action/doSearch?ConceptID=291371&amp;ref=fulltext" title="Electrodes" data-id="article_abstract_Subject_Electrodes" class="article__tags__link">Electrodes</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"><a href="/action/doSearch?ConceptID=292506&amp;ref=fulltext" title="Materials" data-id="article_abstract_Subject_Materials" class="article__tags__header"><h3 class="article__tags__heading">Keywords</h3><div class="article__tags__tooltip" tabindex="0"><div class="article__tags__icon" aria-describedby="tooltip-keywords"><i class="icon-info-circle-outline"></i><span class="sr-only">what are keywords</span></div><p class="article__tags__diff" id="tooltip-keywords" role="tooltip">
                        Article keywords are supplied by the authors and highlight key terms and topics
                        of the paper.
                    </p></div></header><ul class="article__tags__list"><li class="article__tags__item"><a class="article__tags__link" href="https://pubs.acs.org/action/doSearch?action=search&amp;AllField=Sodium-ion+Batteries&amp;qsSearchArea=AllField&amp;ref=fulltext" data-id="article_abstract_Keyword_sodium-ion%20batteries">sodium-ion batteries</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"> <a class="article__tags__link" href="https://pubs.acs.org/action/doSearch?action=search&amp;AllField=In+Situ+Heat+Generation&amp;qsSearchArea=AllField&amp;ref=fulltext" data-id="article_abstract_Keyword_in%20situ%20heat%20generation">in situ heat generation</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"> <a class="article__tags__link" href="https://pubs.acs.org/action/doSearch?action=search&amp;AllField=Full+Cell&amp;qsSearchArea=AllField&amp;ref=fulltext" data-id="article_abstract_Keyword_full%20cell">full cell</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"> <a class="article__tags__link" href="https://pubs.acs.org/action/doSearch?action=search&amp;AllField=Oxyflurophosphate+Cathode&amp;qsSearchArea=AllField&amp;ref=fulltext" data-id="article_abstract_Keyword_oxyflurophosphate%20cathode">oxyflurophosphate cathode</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"> <a class="article__tags__link" href="https://pubs.acs.org/action/doSearch?action=search&amp;AllField=Iron+Doping&amp;qsSearchArea=AllField&amp;ref=fulltext" data-id="article_abstract_Keyword_iron%20doping">iron doping</a></li></ul></div></div></div><div class="article_content"><div class="article_content-table hlFld-FullText"><div class="article_content-row"><div class="article_content-left" property="articleBody"><div id="sec1" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_1"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" tabindex="0"><h2 id="_i2">Introduction</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div></div></div><hr><div class="NLM_p">Sodium-ion batteries (NaIBs) are promising candidates for large-scale energy storage such as grid storage systems because of their low-cost advantages. However, large-scale commercial deployment of NaIBs remains a significant challenge owing to bottlenecks resulting from development of suitable and eco-friendly cathode materials that can enable high power, high energy density, and long cycle life. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref1 ref2 ref3 ref4 ref5 ref6 ref7 ref8'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref1 ref2 ref3 ref4 ref5 ref6 ref7 ref8" aria-label="reference 1 to 8">(1−8)</a> To address this challenge, several cathode chemistries that feature vanadium phosphate-based materials, owing to high performance, excellent structural, and thermal stability, have been extensively studied by researchers as potential and promising cathode candidates in NaIBs. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref4 ref5 ref6 ref9'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref4 ref5 ref6 ref9" aria-label="reference 4 to 6 and 9">(4−6,9)</a> Cathode classes with a phosphate framework containing V<sup>4+</sup> and V<sup>3+</sup> with the general formula Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>2</sub>F<sub>3–<i>x</i></sub>O<sub><i>x</i></sub>, <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref9'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref9" aria-label="reference 9">(9)</a> NaVOPO<sub>4</sub>, <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref10 ref11'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref10 ref11" aria-label="reference 10 and 11">(10,11)</a><sup>,</sup> NaVPO<sub>4</sub>F, <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref12'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref12" aria-label="reference 12">(12)</a> Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub>, <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref13'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref13" aria-label="reference 13">(13)</a> Na<sub>4</sub>VO(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>2</sub>, <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref14'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref14" aria-label="reference 14">(14)</a> Na<sub>7</sub>V<sub>4</sub>(P<sub>2</sub>O<sub>7</sub>)<sub>4</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>), <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref15'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref15" aria-label="reference 15">(15)</a> and Na<sub>3</sub>V(PO<sub>3</sub>)<sub>3</sub>N <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref16'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref16" aria-label="reference 16">(16)</a> are of particular interest owing to their excellent electrochemical performance and cycling stabilities because of their stable structure. Building off of these frameworks, in the recent years, researchers have begun exploring the mixed polyanion with the general formulation Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>2</sub>F<sub>3–<i>x</i></sub>O<sub><i>x</i></sub> for high-energy density NaIBs. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref17'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref17" aria-label="reference 17">(17)</a> During charge/discharge, these materials show the presence of two different redox couples at ∼3.7 and ∼4.1 V, which are higher than the usual ∼3.3 V redox observed for most Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub>-type materials and most other sodium metal oxide cathodes. Over the years, several synthesis routes have been explored to synthesize these materials with the goal to further increase their energy/power densities and improve cycling stabilities, including solid-state, spray-drying, sol–gel, and hydrothermal approaches, each route yielding varying degrees of successes. For example, Xu et al. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref18'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref18" aria-label="reference 18">(18)</a> synthesized the Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>O<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>2</sub>F/reduced-graphene oxide sandwich structure material using the hydrothermal method with <i>N</i>,<i>N</i>-dimethylformamide solvent and NH<sub>4</sub>VO<sub>3</sub>, NaF and (NH<sub>4</sub>)<sub>2</sub>HPO<sub>4</sub> precursors resulting in a cathode material that operates at ∼3.7 V. The presence of reduced-graphene oxide improved the electrochemical performance of the cathode material, delivering a discharge capacity of about ∼110 mA h/g, which was sustained for over 200 cycles at C/10 rates in a half-cell configuration. Similarly, Kumar et al. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref19'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref19" aria-label="reference 19">(19)</a> synthesized a Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>O<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>2</sub>F-MWCNT nanocomposite using an ethylene glycol-assisted hydrothermal method. This material showed excellent electrochemical performance with superior cycling stability, delivering a capacity of ∼98 mA h/g at a 0.1 C rate for 120 cycles and 60 mA h/g at a 2 C rate for 1800 cycles.</div><div class="NLM_p last">In this context, the present work focuses on the synthesis of new optimized iron-doped Na<sub>3</sub>Fe<sub>0.3</sub>V<sub>1.7</sub>O(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>2</sub>F<sub>2</sub> cathode material for NaIBs using a new facile hydrothermal route. In the conventional Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>O(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>2</sub>F<sub>2</sub> structure, vanadium displays +3 and +4 oxidation states. As only 2 sodium atoms can be removed from the structure when the cell is charged to 4.5 V, vanadium is not totally oxidized to +5 oxidation state with a theoretical capacity of around ∼130 mA h/g (based on 2Na removal). The authors aim to partially substitute the toxic and expensive vanadium metal by a cheap and environmentally friendly element without impairing the material electrochemical performance and especially its reversible capacity during cycling. The first choice was iron because Fe<sup>3+</sup> and V<sup>3+</sup>, in VI coordination, have a similar ionic radius of 0.645 and 0.64 Å, respectively, making it an ideal candidate as a dopant. The synthesized material was characterized using X-ray diffraction (XRD), scanning electron microscopy (SEM), Mössbauer microscopy, and transmission electron microscopy techniques. The electrochemical performances were evaluated using charge/discharge cycling and electrochemical impedance spectroscopy (EIS). Additionally, an electrochemical isothermal calorimetry measurement was performed on the Na/Na<sub>3</sub>Fe<sub>0.3</sub>V<sub>1.7</sub>O(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>2</sub>F<sub>2</sub> half-cell to investigate the impact of state of charge (SOC), charge/discharge rate, and temperature on heat generation and to describe the material thermal behavior during cycling. Overall, this work provides a new synthesis route for the development of iron-doped sodium vanadium oxyflurophosphate high-performance sodium-based material in large-scale energy storage based on sodium battery systems.</div></div><div id="sec2" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_1"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" tabindex="0"><h2 id="_i3">Experimental Section</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div></div></div><hr><div class="NLM_p">The Na<sub>3</sub>Fe<sub>0.3</sub>V<sub>1.7</sub>O(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>2</sub>F<sub>2</sub> material was successfully prepared using a single step via a hydrothermal route without any heat treatments according to the previously reported procedures. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref20'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref20" aria-label="reference 20">(20)</a> The specific composition was chosen on the basis of achieving good phase purity and enhanced electrochemical performance. The detailed synthesis method has been discussed in our previous report. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref3'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref3" aria-label="reference 3">(3)</a> Stoichiometric mixtures of NH<sub>4</sub>VO<sub>3</sub> (Aldrich, ≥99.99%), acetic acid CH<sub>3</sub>COOH (Aldrich, ≥99.99%), NaF (Aldrich, ≥99%), Fe(NO<sub>3</sub>)<sub>3</sub>·9H<sub>2</sub>O (Aldrich, ≥99%), and NH<sub>4</sub>H<sub>2</sub>PO<sub>4</sub> (Aldrich, 99.99%) were used in the synthesis. Initially, a clear green solution (solution A) was prepared by dissolving a 1:1 mol ratio of NH<sub>4</sub>VO<sub>3</sub> and acetic acid (CH<sub>3</sub>COOH) in 20 mL of DI water. This was followed by dissolving Fe(NO<sub>3</sub>)<sub>3</sub>·9H<sub>2</sub>O in solution A which was stirred at 70 °C for 30 min. Solution B was then prepared by adding NaF and NH<sub>4</sub>H<sub>2</sub>PO<sub>4</sub> to 10 mL of DI water. After stirring at 70 °C for 30 min, solution B was added to solution A dropwise to form a new mixture, which was stirred at 70 °C for an additional 1 h. Then, the final mixed solution was transferred to a 100 mL autoclave which was then heated in a hot air oven at 200 °C for 24 h. Finally, after the hydrothermal treatment, a green powder was obtained after filtration. This was then dried under vacuum at 100 °C for a period of 12 h.</div><div id="sec2_1" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_2"><div id="ac_i4" class="anchor-spacer"></div><h3 class="article-section__title" id="_i4"> Powder XRD and SEM Measurements</h3><div class="NLM_p last">Powder XRD measurements were performed using a Bruker D8 diffractometer in the Bragg–Brentano reflection geometry equipped with a 1.6 kW sealed X-ray tube source (Cu Kα radiation) with a Vantec-2000 2D detector to identify the phase purity of the as-synthesized materials between 10 and 80° (2θ value). Full pattern matching was performed on the obtained diffraction patterns with the Jana2006 program package. The particle size and morphology were characterized using a field-emission scanning electron microscope (FEI, Quanta 650). A transmission electron microscope (Talos F200X, FEI) with a 200 kV operating voltage was used to capture the morphology, energy-dispersive X-ray spectroscopy (EDX) spectrum, and selected area electron diffraction patterns of the Na<sub>3</sub>Fe<sub>0.3</sub>V<sub>1.7</sub>O(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>2</sub>F<sub>2</sub> composite.</div></div><div id="sec2_2" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_2"><div id="ac_i5" class="anchor-spacer"></div><h3 class="article-section__title" id="_i5"> Mössbauer Spectroscopy</h3><div class="NLM_p last">The <sup>57</sup>Fe Mössbauer spectroscopy spectrum was recorded in ambient air at room temperature in transmission geometry and the constant accelerator mode with a <sup>57</sup>Co source in an Rh matrix. The source was kept in ambient temperature and the experimental spectrum was recorded in the ±4 mm/s velocity range. The velocity scale was calibrated with the magnetically split sextet spectrum of a high-purity iron foil as the reference absorber. The Mössbauer absorber was prepared with 40 mg/cm<sup>2</sup> by mixing the material with boron nitride. The Mössbauer parameters were determined by fitting the experimental data with one Lorentzian doublet using the Fulham program. The validity of the fit was evaluated based on minimizing the number of parameters and χ<sup>2</sup> values. The value of the isomer shift is given with respect to α-Fe.</div></div><div id="sec2_3" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_2"><div id="ac_i6" class="anchor-spacer"></div><h3 class="article-section__title" id="_i6"> Electrochemical Cycling</h3><div class="NLM_p last">Positive electrodes were prepared from mixtures containing 80 wt % active materials, 10 wt % acetylene black, and 10 wt % polyvinylidene difluorides in <i>N</i>-methyl-2-pyrrolidone as a solvent. The electrodes were prepared by casting the slurry onto aluminum foil with a doctor blade and drying in a vacuum oven at 110 °C overnight under vacuum. The resulting electrode film was pressed with a twin roller, cut into a round plate (Φ = 14.5 mm), and dried at 120 °C for 12 h under vacuum. All the electrochemical performances were carried out using coin-type cells with Whatman fiber glass separators, which were assembled in an argon-filled glovebox. The electrochemical properties were evaluated using galvanostatic techniques in the voltage window of 2.8–4.5 V (vs Na/Na<sup>+</sup>) at room temperature and 45 °C and in various electrolytes such as 1 M NaPF<sub>6</sub> dissolved in ethylene carbonate (EC)–propylene carbonate (PC) (1/1), EC–PC–dimethyl carbonate (DMC) (2:5:3), and EC–diethyl carbonate (DEC) (1:1) in the volume ratio. All the solvents and salt were purchased from Sigma-Aldrich.</div></div><div id="sec2_4" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_2"><div id="ac_i7" class="anchor-spacer"></div><h3 class="article-section__title" id="_i7"> Galvanostatic Intermittent Titration Technique and EIS Measurements</h3><div class="NLM_p">The equivalent current of the C/20 rate was applied during charging/discharging cycling using a Solartron battery cycler (1470E). Detailed discussion about the experimental procedure is found elsewhere. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref21'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref21" aria-label="reference 21">(21)</a> The cell was charged and discharged stepwise. In every step, the current was applied for 2 h and then the cell rested for 3 h to attain the steady-state cell voltage. The measurement was repeated at least twice. When the cell voltage decay was less than 2 mV/h under the open-circuit voltage (OCV) condition, the EIS measurements were performed in the frequency range between 2 MHz and 5 mHz. A sinusoidal voltage amplitude of 10 mV was applied during EIS data acquisition and fitted with an equivalent circuit.</div><div class="NLM_p">In the single particle of Na<sub>3</sub>Fe<sub>0.3</sub>V<sub>1.7</sub>O(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>2</sub>F<sub>2</sub>, the sodium depleted from its surface in the charging process and a concentration gradient was generated between the surface and bulk. This condition resulted in a cell voltage polarization with applied current. Under the OCV condition, the polarized cell voltage slowly relaxed with time. The relaxation time was obtained from depolarization voltage versus time derivative. The diffusion length was determined based on the particle diameter.</div><div class="NLM_p last">Ionic diffusivity was measured as a function of temperature at fixed sodium content (Na<sub>2</sub>Fe<sub>0.3</sub>V<sub>1.7</sub>O(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>2</sub>F<sub>2</sub>). The cell was charged for 2 h and relaxed for 3 h as in the procedure mentioned above and again discharged for 2 h to obtain the same composition (Na<sub>2</sub>Fe<sub>0.3</sub>V<sub>1.7</sub>O(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>2</sub>F<sub>2</sub>). The measurement was repeated for temperatures from 0 to 50 °C with 10 °C intervals. Under the OCV conditions, the EIS measurements were also performed as a function of temperature after cell relaxation.</div></div><div id="sec2_5" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_2"><div id="ac_i8" class="anchor-spacer"></div><h3 class="article-section__title" id="_i8"> Electrochemical Isothermal Calorimetry Measurement</h3><div class="NLM_p last">The isothermal calorimetry system (TAM IV micro-calorimeter system, TA Instruments) coupled with an external Arbin Instrument battery cycler (model BT-2000) was used to measure the heat generation of the Na/Na<sub>3</sub>Fe<sub>0.3</sub>V<sub>1.7</sub>O(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>2</sub>F<sub>2</sub> coin-type half-cells during charge/discharge processes at 25 and 45 °C. The cell was fitted in the sample holder at the specimen side of the calorimeter and connected to the battery cycler through two pairs of wires for charge and discharge. It was isolated adiabatically from the surroundings. The heat generation output was the differential value between the sample and the inert reference. To examine the effect of the charge/discharge rate on heat generation, the cells were cycled between a 2 and 4.5 V cutoff voltage at three different rates (0.1 C, 0.2 C, and 1.0 C) for 25 °C and at 0.2 and 1.0 C for 45 °C. Measurements were performed three times at each temperature and cycling rate to assess the reproducibility.</div></div></div><div id="sec3" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_1"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" tabindex="0"><h2 id="_i9">Results and Discussion</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div></div></div><hr><div class="NLM_p">The synthesized Na<sub>3</sub>Fe<sub>0.3</sub>V<sub>1.7</sub>O(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>2</sub>F<sub>2</sub> cathode material was first analyzed using powder XRD. The diffractogram of the material recorded in the 2-theta range of 10–70° is illustrated in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">1</a>a. The XRD pattern confirms the high purity of the synthesized Na<sub>3</sub>Fe<sub>0.3</sub>V<sub>1.7</sub>O(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>2</sub>F<sub>2</sub> material without the presence of any crystalline impurities. All peaks are sharp and well-defined, confirming the high degree of crystallinity of Na<sub>3</sub>Fe<sub>0.3</sub>V<sub>1.7</sub>O(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>2</sub>F<sub>2</sub>. The chemical composition of Na<sub>3</sub>Fe<sub>0.3</sub>V<sub>1.7</sub>O(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>2</sub>F<sub>2</sub> was qualitatively confirmed by EDX analysis (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">1</a>b). Full pattern matching indicated that the material had an orthorhombic crystal structure with the space group Amam similar to Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>O(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>2</sub>F<sub>2</sub> reported by Nguyen et al. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref22'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref22" aria-label="reference 22">(22)</a> The calculated lattice parameters were <i>a</i> = 9.041(1) Å, <i>b</i> = 9.039(1) Å, and <i>c</i> = 10.631(1) Å which are very similar to those reported by several authors (<a class="ref showTableEvent internalNav" data-id="tbl1" href="#tbl1">Table </a><a class="ref showTableEvent internalNav" data-id="tbl1" href="#tbl1">1</a>). The absence of impurity phases confirms the successful partial replacement of vanadium by iron and was confirmed by EDX analysis (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">1</a>b).</div><figure id="fig1" data-index="1" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 1</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.0c11616/asset/images/medium/am0c11616_0002.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.0c11616/asset/images/large/am0c11616_0002.jpeg" id="gr1" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 1. (a) Full pattern matching results of the XRD pattern, (b) EDX spectrum, and (c,d) SEM image of the synthesized Na<sub>3</sub>Fe<sub>0.3</sub>V<sub>1.7</sub>O(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>2</sub>F<sub>2</sub> powder by the hydrothermal method.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsami.0c11616/asset/images/large/am0c11616_0002.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsami.0c11616&amp;id=fig1"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><div class="NLM_table-wrap" id="tbl1"><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption"><div class="NLM_caption" id=""><div class="title2">Table 1. return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref23" aria-label="reference 23">(23)</a></td></tr><tr valign="top" class="colsep0"><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" scope="row" align="left">Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>O (PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>2</sub>F<sub>2</sub></td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="left">9.035(1)</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="left">9.037(1)</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="left">10.686(1)</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="left"> <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref22');
