        </div><div class="casAbstract">A Na3V2O2(PO4)2F/reduced-graphene-oxide (RGO) sandwich structure was synthesized by a facile one-step solvothermal method.  Cubic Na3V2O2(PO4)2F nanoparticles are homogeneously trapped between conductive RGO sheets during its growth and assembled into a compact sandwich structure, which allows the elec. insulating Na3V2O2(PO4)2F nanoparticles to be wired up to a current collector through the underlying graphene conducting layers.                         cas_cit19R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">19</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Na3V2O2(PO4)2F-MWCNT nanocomposites as a stable and high rate cathode for aqueous and non-aqueous sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Kumar, P. Ramesh; Jung, Young Hwa; Wang, Ji Eun; Kim, Do Kyung</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Power Sources</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">324</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">NASICON-type structured Na3V2O2(PO4)2F nanocubes with multi-wall carbon nanotubes (MWCNTs) composite has been synthesized by ethylene glycol-assisted hydrothermal reaction and used as a rechargeable non-aq. and aq. sodium-ion battery cathode material.  As a cathode material for non-aq. sodium-ion batteries, as-synthesized Na3V2O2(PO4)2F-MWCNT composite shows stable capacity of 98 mAh g-1 at 0.1 C for 120 cycles and 60 mAh g-1 at 2 C for 1800 cycles in half-cell and full-cell configurations, resp.  In aq. electrolytes, Na3V2O2(PO4)2F-MWCNT composite delivers discharge capacity of 35 mAh g-1 at 1 C rate in half-cell and 42 mAh g-1 at 1 C rate in full-cell with NaTi2(PO4)3-MWCNT as an anode.  Stable cyclability and high rate performance of Na3V2O2(PO4)2F-MWCNT nanocomposite can be attributed to the very short sodium ion diffusion length in nano cube morphol. of Na3V2O2(PO4)2F as well as the carbon nanotubes matrix which endows the unbreakable conductive networks for electrons and Na+ ions.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrpvO0xa2dxJrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgcGNAqCSUHUA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XovV2iu74%253D&amp;md5=4598319afcdf7384ec075d375466a43f</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref20"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref20'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">20</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit20"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Essehli, R.</span>; <span class="NLM_string-name">Yahia, H.                         cas_cit21R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">21</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Extreme fast charging characteristics of zirconia modified LiNi0.5Mn1.5O4 cathode for lithium ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Nisar, Umair; Amin, Ruhul; Essehli, Rachid; Shakoor, R. A.; Kahraman, Ramazan; Kim, Do Kyung; Khaleel, Mohammad A.; Belharouak, Ilias</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Power Sources</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">396</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">774-781</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JPSODZ</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">LiNi0.5Mn1.5O4 is a promising high-voltage cathode for Li-ion battery fast charging applications.  Aware of its electrochem. stability issues, the material's surface is modified with small amts. of zirconia (ZrO2) ranging from 0.5 to 2% using a scalable ball milling process.  The advantage of the coating was demonstrated in electrochem. measurements performed at room temp. and 55°, and in cells discharged under high-rate conditions up to 80C.  Of significance, the material coated with 1.0% ZrO2 was cycled at the 40C rate for over a thousand cycles and retains 86% of its initial capacity.  The material with 2.0% ZrO2 modification preserves 76% of its initial capacity when cycled at the 40C rate and 55°.  The coated materials showed excellent cycling stability when subjected to 6C (10-min) fast charging and C/3 discharging for 300 cycles.  Compared to the uncoated material, the interfacial resistance of the zirconia modified LiNi0.5Mn1.5O4 is much lower and does not significantly increase with increasing the coating amt.  However, the electrochem. performances are still partly limited by both interfacial resistance at the beginning of charge and electrolyte diffusivity, particularly under higher rate cycling conditions.  Overall, the strategy of ZrO2 surface modification applied to LiNi0.5Mn1.5O4 unveils the potential that the material could play in extreme fast charged elec. vehicles.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqCAsGTw-LlybVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljHxh-WmtQrFw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXht1ertrzE&amp;md5=432c74d64609b07d9358012eedfc99cf</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref22"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref22'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">22</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit22" data-doi="10.1016/j.ensm.2019.04.010"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Nguyen, L.                         cas_cit23R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">23</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Phase-pure Na3V2(PO4)2F3 embedded in carbon matrix through a facile polyol synthesis as a potential cathode for high performance sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Park, Sohyun; Song, Jinju; Kim, Seyeon; Sambandam, Balaji; Mathew, Vinod; Kim, Sungjin; Jo, Jeonggeun; Kim, Seokhun; Kim, Jaekook</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Research</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2019</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">12</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">4</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">911-917</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Springer GmbH</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">In this study, a pseudo-layered Na super-ionic conductor of Na3V2(PO4)2F3 (NVPF)/C cathode for sodium-ion batteries is prepd. successfully using a facile polyol refluxing process without any impurity phases.  The X-ray diffraction and Rietveld refinement results confirm that NVPF possesses tetragonal NASICON-type lattice with a space group of P42/mnm.  In this preparative method, polyol is utilized as a solvent as well as a carbon source.  The presence of nanosized NVPF particles in the carbon network is confirmed by field-emission SEM (FE-SEM) and high-resoln. transmission electron microscopy (HR-TEM).  The existence of carbon is analyzed by Raman scattering and elemental anal.  When applied as a Na-storage material in a potential window of 2.0-4.3 V, the electrode exhibits two flat voltage plateaus at 3.7 and 4.2 V with an electrochem. active V3+/V4+ redox couple.  In addn., Na3V2(PO4)2F3/C composite achieved a retention capacity of ∼ 88% even after 1,500 cycles at 15 C.  Moreover, at high current densities of 30 and 50 C, Na3V2(PO4)2F3/C cathode retains the specific discharge capacities of 108.4 and 105.9 mAh·g-1, resp., revealing the structural stability of the material prepd. through a facile polyol refluxing method.                         cas_cit24R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">24</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Iron-Doped Sodium-Vanadium Fluorophosphates: Na3V2-yO2-yFey(PO4)2F1+y (y &lt; 0.3)</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Palomares, Veronica; Iturrondobeitia, Amaia; Sanchez-Fontecoba, Paula; Goonetilleke, Damian; Sharma, Neeraj; Lezama, Luis; Rojo, Teofilo</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Inorganic Chemistry</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">59</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">1</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">854-862</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">INOCAJ</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0020-1669</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The Na-V fluorophosphate family was actively studied recently, but few examples tackle chem. doping or the substitution of V.  This work presents Fe-doped compds. Na3V2-yO2-yFey(PO4)2F1+y (y ≤ 0.3) prepd. by hydrothermal synthesis with low Fe content.  The amt. of Fe in the structure is confirmed by x-ray and neutron powder diffraction, electronic paramagnetic resonance, magnetic susceptibility measurements, and solid-state NMR (ssNMR).  The degree of V substitution, together with the soly. limit for Fe in Na-V fluorophosphates, was calcd. by ssNMR and magnetic susceptibility measurements to be y = 0.3 based on the synthetic route used here.  The introduction of small amts. of Fe3+ to the structure leads to the redn. of a fraction of V4+ to V3+, and the voltage profiles do not change with the introduction of Fe to the structure.  In situ synchrotron x-ray diffraction demonstrates that the electrochem.-structural changes during charge and discharge are very similar to those obsd. in the V3+/V4+ mixed-valent Na3V2O1.6(PO4)2F1.4, which could be related to the existence of both Fe dopant and V3+ in the phase.  This work presents Na-V fluorophosphates derived from the substitution of V in Na3(VO)2(PO4)2F with a low amt. of a trivalent species such as Fe3+.  Doping leads to V3+/4+ mixed valence and affects the magnetic and spectroscopic properties that can be related to the electrochem. performance of these compds., avoiding the loss of specific capacity assocd. with Na3Fe2(PO4)2F3.  The structural evolution of the Fe-doped samples is also explored in situ while running in a Na-ion half-cell.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGp_6_-O5jAXY7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljHxh-WmtQrFw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1MXitlymtr7L&amp;md5=ddcad0b911067c8d26beccd3699886f1</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref25"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref25'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">25</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit25" data-doi="10.1016/j.jssc.2019.121010"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shakhova, I.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Rozova, M.         </div><div class="casAbstract">The Na3V2-yFeyO2x(PO4)2F3-2x (x = 1 - 0.8, y = 0 - 0.8) solid solns. were prepd. using a microwave-assisted hydrothermal technique.  The materials crystallize in the disordered I4/mmm crystal structure as evidenced with electron diffraction and Rietveld refinement from powder x-ray diffraction data (Na3V1.2Fe0.8O1.6(PO4)2F1.4: a 6.38666(9), c 10.6562(2) Å, R = 0.023, RP = 0.013).  A combination of EELS and 57Fe Mossbauer spectroscopy revealed that V is in the mixed 4+/5+ oxidn. state, whereas Fe is exclusively in the 3+ state, thus pointing to the V4+ → Fe3+/V5+ co-substitution.  The solid solns. demonstrate reversible Na+ (de)intercalation in the electrochem. cells with Na metal counter-electrode through two sloping potential plateaus at ∼3.5 and 4.0 V vs. Na+/Na.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Ambient temp. Na-ion batteries are alternatives to com. dominant Li-ion batteries for larger scale stationary applications.  To realize such a Na-ion battery, electrodes need to be developed, understood, and improved.  Here, Na3V2O2(PO4)2F is studied from the perspective of Na.  Reaction mechanisms for this cathode during battery function include the following: (a) a region comprising at least 3 phases with subtly varying Na compns. that transform via 2 2-phase reaction mechanisms, which appears at the lower potential plateau-like region during both charge and discharge; an extended solid soln. region for majority of the cycling process, including most of the higher potential plateau; and (b) a 2nd 2-phase region near the highest charge state during charge and between the 1st and 2nd plateau-like regions during discharge.  Notably, the distinct asymmetry in the reaction mechanism, lattice, and vol. evolution on charge relative to discharge manifests an interesting question: Is such an asymmetry beneficial for this cathode.  These reaction mechanisms are inherently related to Na evolution, which shows complex behavior between the 2 Na crystallog. sites in this compd. that in turn mediate the lattice and reaction evolution.  Thus, this work relates at.-level Na perturbations directly with electrochem. cycling.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrRcmTn-6AIp7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgGwYbJtVyHHQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXnvV2gsrY%253D&amp;md5=6ae04aee9e95d16b3d91f0138cf7f09a</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref27"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref27'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">27</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit27" data-doi="10.1039/c7ra01047h"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kumar, P.                         cas_cit31R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">31</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Assessment of the Electrochemical Stability of Carbonate-Based Electrolytes in Na-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yan, Guochun; Alves-Dalla-Corte, Daniel; Yin, Wei; Madern, Nathalie; Gachot, Gregory; Tarascon, Jean-Marie</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of the Electrochemical Society</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">The large abundance of Na combined with the feasibility of Na-based insertion compds., such as Na3V2(PO4)2F3, makes the Na-ion battery an attractive technol. compared with Li-ion battery for a few applications.  Nonetheless, one identified limitation of the Na3V2(PO4)2F3/HC system is its poor long-term cycling performance at elevated temp., hence the sorely need to screen the proper electrolyte formulation.  Here, we report a thorough survey aiming to assess the pros and cons of cyclic vs. linear carbonates with respect to the performances of Na3V2(PO4)2F3/HC cells.  Through complementary in-situ UV and CV anal. techniques we reveal the formation of sol. species stemming from the partial decompn. of linear carbonates (DMC and EMC) in redn. into sol. products, hence stressing their failure to provide a stable solid electrolyte interphase (SEI) at the hard carbon electrode and by the same token accounting for the poor performance of the overall cell.  We discuss the decompn. reaction paths, and propose a shuttle mechanism to account for the cell deterioration.  Our results, which underscores the detrimental effects of linear carbonates in full Na-ion Na3V2(PO4)2F3/HC cells, should serve as an impetus to identify superior electrolyte formulation for increasing the high temp. robustness of this technol.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoHtxUKlOUd1bVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lj3LL0HBGIjDg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXhtVWltbrE&amp;md5=c2a2599dc83def3f1133c49154b7f596</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref32"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref32'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">32</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit32" data-doi="10.1149/2.0831802jes"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yan, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Dugas, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tarascon, J.-M.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">The Na3V2(PO4)2F3/Carbon Na-Ion Battery: Its Performance Understanding as Deduced from Differential Voltage Analysis</span>. <i>J.         </div><div class="casAbstract">The Na3V2(PO4)2F3/Carbon Na-ion battery technol. is appealing because of its high energy and power d., hence the need to assess its viability under practical operation.  Here a comprehensive understanding is provided of its storage and cycling performances in various electrolytes and at different temps. via a through differential voltage (dV/dQ) anal. of the data obtained from coin and pouch cells.  The cells show excellent long-term cycling performance (capacity decay less than 0.020 mAh g-1 per cycle at 1C rate whatever the electrolytes), but suffer at 55°C from copious self-discharge stemming from either redn. or oxidization of electrolytes.  It is deduced, from monitoring side reactions rate as a function of temp., the activation energies of 34 and 29 kJ mol-1 for the parasitic reactions proceeding at the anode and cathode side, resp. Na4Ni3(PO4)2P2O7 exhibits the highest Ni3+/Ni2+ redox potential of 4.8 V vs.  Na+/Na with a theor. capacity of 127 mAh g-1.  Here, we report on the synthesis and characterizations of Na4Ni3(PO4)2P2O7-reduced graphene oxide and Na4Ni3(PO4)2P2O7-carbon composites. In this study, we prepd. different composites of sodium cobalt mixed-phosphate with multiwalled carbon nanotubes (Na4Co3(PO4)2P2O7-MWCNTs) by the sol-gel synthesis technique.  The crystal structure and microstructure were characterized by using PXRD, TGA, Raman spectroscopy, SEM and TEM.  The electrochem. properties of the Na4Co3(PO4)2P2O7-20 wt% MWCNT composite were explored using two different electrolytes.  The composite electrode exhibited excellent cyclability and rate capabilities with the electrolyte composed of 1 M sodium hexafluorophosphate in ethylene carbonate:dimethyl carbonate (EC:DMC).  The composite electrode delivered stable discharge capacities of 80 mA h g-1 and 78 mA h g-1 at room and elevated (55°C) temps., resp.  The av. discharge voltage was around 4.45 V vs. Na+/Na, which corresponded to the Co2+/3+ redox couple.  The feasibility of the Na4Co3(PO4)2P2O7 cathode for sodium-ion batteries has been confirmed in real time using a full cell configuration vs.  NaTi2(PO4)3-20 wt% MWCNT, and it delivers an initial discharge capacity of 78 mA h g-1.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrogKZ-10bfnbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lj3LL0HBGIjDg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXns1Cgsbk%253D&amp;md5=dabc05eb6816c624af55ce0c6bf42844</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref36"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref36'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">36</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit36" data-doi="10.1002/0470020229"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Maier, J.</span></span> <i>Physical Chemistry of Ionic Materials: Ions and Electrons in Solids</i>; <span class="NLM_publisher-name">John Wiley &amp; Sons</span>, <span class="NLM_year">2004</span>.</span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26publication_year%3D2004%26author%3DJ.%2BMaier%26title%3DPhysical%2BChemistry%2Bof%2BIonic%2BMaterials%253A%2BIons%2Band%2BElectrons%2Bin%2BSolids&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.0c11616&amp;doiOfLink=10.1002%2F0470020229&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord empty" id="

                        cas_cit38R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">38</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">A High Power-High Energy Na3V2(PO4)2F3 Sodium Cathode: Investigation of Transport Parameters, Rational Design and Realization</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhu, Changbao; Wu, Chao; Chen, Chia-Chin; Kopold, Peter; van Aken, Peter A.; Maier, Joachim; Yu, Yan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemistry of Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">29</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">12</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">5207-5215</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">CMATEX</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0897-4756</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium ion batteries are realistic and promising alternatives to lithium due to the abundance of Na and the similar intercalation chem. of Na when compared to the lithium counterpart.  Developing high-power and high-energy sodium batteries is still a significant challenge.  Na3V2(PO4)2F3 (NVPF) has been shown to combine excellent charge-discharge kinetics with a competitively high voltage.  However, the major issue is, as for the vast majority of electrode materials, the lack of distinct knowledge of fundamental transport parameters, on which an optimized strategy for developing a high-power and high-energy sodium cathode can be based.  This work aims at filling this gap.  We exptl. investigate the intrinsic ionic and electronic conductivities, as well as the chem. diffusion coeff. of sodium of Na3V2(PO4)2F3 by impedance and dc polarization.  On the basis of these results, we develop an optimized design.  As the electronic cond. is found to be much smaller than the ionic one, electronic wiring of the particles (by a graphene network) has higher priority than providing electrolyte contact.  This is important since the contact by graphene and electrolyte wetting is partly antagonistic, not so much because of interfacial tensions rather because of the introduced heterogeneities on the nanoscale (cf. Lotus effect).  We develop and apply a one-step cost-effective low temp. hydrothermal method without any postheat treatment for the fabrication of a nanoparticulate (∼30-50 nm) NVPF electrode, which provides sufficient porosity and in which every nanoparticle is connected to the graphene network.  In terms of rate capability, the performance of this electrode is excellent and at least belongs to the best Na storage performances reported for Na3V2(PO4)2F3 so far.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGojv-JE23Bt6LVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhJcHu8iZ3YPA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXos1alurg%253D&amp;md5=a1aee1a498a19ac1ba20d70532253a9c</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref39"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref39'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">39</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit39" data-doi="10.1149/1.1387224"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kim, J.-S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Prakash, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Selman, J.                         cas_cit39R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">39</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Thermal characteristics of LixMn2O4 spinel</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Kim, Jeom-Soo; Prakash, Jai; Selman, J. R.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Electrochemical and Solid-State Letters</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2001</span>),

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Electrochemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The heat generation characteristics of LixMn2O4 spinel as a pos. electrode material were measured in situ during cycling of Li/LixMn2O4 cell, using an isothermal microcalorimeter in combination with a battery tester.  The total heat generation rate is dependent on the concn. of lithium in LixMn2O4.  By sepg. irreversible heat from the total heat rate, using dc interruption technique, the concn. dependence is shown to be mainly due to the reversible heat of the cell, which shows a cooling-heating-cooling-heating cycle, during charge/discharge.  This thermal characteristic may be explained from the phase diagram of LixMn2O4, in agreement with recent reports on the phase-change behavior.  The dependence of the thermal characteristics on the current level is weak at a low C rate, but increases steeply from C/3 to 1C rate.  Although voltage profiles of charge and discharge showed similar behavior, the range of discontinuity (between 4.1 and 4.0 V) is not identical for charge and discharge.  While the voltage profile is affected by irreversibility (charge vs. discharge), the thermal profile is barely affected by it.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrVY1wam6IjubVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhJcHu8iZ3YPA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BD3MXmtFegsbY%253D&amp;md5=451bcf7f80963ca9ad96f33043c9b43c</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref40"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref40'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">40</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit40" data-doi="10.1149/1.1541672"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lu, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Prakash, J.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">In Situ Measurements of Heat Generation in a Li/Mesocarbon Microbead Half-Cell</span>. <i>J.                 10.1016/j.electacta.2005.06.028</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D51%26publication_year%3D2006%26pages%3D1322%26journal%3DElectrochim.%2BActa%26author%3DW.%2BLu%26author%3DH.%2BYang%26author%3DJ.%2BPrakash%26title%3DDetermination%2Bof%2Bthe%2BReversible%2Band%2BIrreversible%2BHeats%2Bof%2BLini%2B%257BSub%2B0.8%257D%2BCo%2B%257BSub%2B0.2%257D%2BO%2B%257BSub%2B2%257D%252FMesocarbon%2BMicrobead%2BLi-Ion%2BCell%2BReactions%2BUsing%2BIsothermal%2BMicrocalorimetery%26doi%3D10.1016%252Fj.electacta.2005.06.028&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.0c11616&amp;doiOfLink=10.1016%2Fj.electacta.2005.06.028&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit42R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">42</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Determination of the reversible and irreversible heats of LiNi0.8Co0.2O2/mesocarbon microbead Li-ion cell reactions using isothermal microcalorimetery</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Lu, Wenquan; Yang, Hui; Prakash, Jai</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Electrochimica Acta</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2006</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">51</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">7</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1322-1329</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ELCAAV</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0013-4686</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Cyclic voltammetry of a LiNi0.8Co0.2O2/Li half-cell and a mesocarbon microbead (MCMB)/Li half-cell were studied at low scan rates.  The thermal behavior of these 2 half-cells and a LiNi0.8Co0.2O2/MCMB full-cell cycled at different currents was studied with an electrochem.-microcalorimeter technique in terms of reversible and irreversible heat generation.  The results agreed with the exptl. data at low and moderate currents (≤C/4).  The quant. heat contribution of the cathode and anode to the overall cell heat generation was also detd.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpDE2Sk61PGc7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lig-kWg5kcW2g"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BD2MXhtlertbbO&amp;md5=44ef3e10c31114f4e19aff0fd2291883</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref43"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref43'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">43</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit43" data-doi="10.1016/j.applthermaleng.2017.04.077"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Du, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lai, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ai, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ai, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cheng, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jia, M.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">An Investigation of Irreversible Heat Generation in Lithium Ion Batteries Based on a Thermo-Electrochemical Coupling Method</span>. <i>Appl. Therm. Eng.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2017</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>121</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">501</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">510</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1016/j.applthermaleng.2017.04.077</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D121%26publication_year%3D2017%26pages%3D501-510%26journal%3DAppl.%2BTherm.%2BEng.%26author%3DS.%2BDu%26author%3DY.%2BLai%26author%3DL.%2BAi%26author%3DL.%2BAi%26author%3DY.%2BCheng%26author%3DY.%2BTang%26author%3DM.%2BJia%26title%3DAn%2BInvestigation%2Bof%2BIrreversible%2BHeat%2BGeneration%2Bin%2BLithium%2BIon%2BBatteries%2BBased%2Bon%2Ba%2BThermo-Electrochemical%2BCoupling%2BMethod%26doi%3D10.1016%252Fj.applthermaleng.2017.04.077&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.0c11616&amp;doiOfLink=10.1016%2Fj.applthermaleng.2017.04.077&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit43R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">43</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">An investigation of irreversible heat generation in lithium ion batteries based on a thermo-electrochemical coupling method</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Du, Shuanglong; Lai, Yanqing; Ai, Liang; Ai, Lihua; Cheng, Yun; Tang, Yiwei; Jia, Ming</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Applied Thermal Engineering</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">121</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">501-510</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ATENFT</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1359-4311</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Irreversible heat generation plays a dominant role in li-ion batteries, it is thus highly important to study its evolution in order to adapt the development of electronic devices.  Internal irreversible heat generation mainly consists of two parts: one arises from the polarization and the other one from ohmic heat generation.  A thermo-electrochem. coupling model was established here to study the prodn. and evolution of the irreversible heat within li-ion batteries considering dynamic parameters and the elec. double layer.  Results show that the irreversible heat prodn. rapidly increases with the discharge rate and the polarization heat prodn. is the dominating factor.  Ohmic heat prodn. mainly resulted in the heating of the electrolyte, and the heating produced at the neg. active materials result to be negligible respect to the one produced at the pos. active materials.  According to calcns., the ratio between the ohmic heat prodn. and the total irreversible heat prodn. increases from 24.2% at 3 C to 32.8% at 8 C, thus, the ratio related to the polarization heating decreases from 75.6% to 67.2%.  In addn., effects of the particle size at the pos. and neg. electrodes at the rate of 3 C were studied.  Results show that the neg. electrode particle size has thus a more significant impact on the irreversible heat prodn. and the polarization heat prodn. of the battery.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpxHMeJYFYdnrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lig-kWg5kcW2g"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXntFemtb0%253D&amp;md5=baa4f07a7946a26020e4051e86b27fc5</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref44"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref44'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">44</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit44" data-doi="10.1007/s10973-013-3599-9"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ouyang, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lu, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Han, X.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Analysis of the Heat Generation of Lithium-Ion Battery During Charging and Discharging Considering Different Influencing Factors</span>. <i>J. Therm. Anal. Calorim.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2014</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>116</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">1001</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">1010</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1007/s10973-013-3599-9</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D116%26publication_year%3D2014%26pages%3D1001-1010%26journal%3DJ.%2BTherm.%2BAnal.%2BCalorim.%26author%3DG.%2BLiu%26author%3DM.%2BOuyang%26author%3DL.%2BLu%26author%3DJ.%2BLi%26author%3DX.%2BHan%26title%3DAnalysis%2Bof%2Bthe%2BHeat%2BGeneration%2Bof%2BLithium-Ion%2BBattery%2BDuring%2BCharging%2Band%2BDischarging%2BConsidering%2BDifferent%2BInfluencing%2BFactors%26doi%3D10.1007%252Fs10973-013-3599-9&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.0c11616&amp;doiOfLink=10.1007%2Fs10973-013-3599-9&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit44R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">44</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Analysis of the heat generation of lithium-ion battery during charging and discharging considering different influencing factors</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liu, Guangming; Ouyang, Minggao; Lu, Languang; Li, Jianqiu; Han, Xuebing</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Thermal Analysis and Calorimetry</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2014</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">116</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">2</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1001-1010</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JTACF7</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1388-6150</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Springer</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Operating temp. of lithium-ion battery is an important factor influencing the performance of elec. vehicles.  During charging and discharging process, battery temp. varies due to internal heat generation, calling for anal. of battery heat generation rate.  The generated heat consists of Joule heat and reaction heat, and both are affected by various factors, including temp., battery aging effect, state of charge (SOC), and operation current.  In this article, a series of expts. based on a power-type lithium manganese oxide/graphite battery was implemented under different conditions.  The parameters for Joule heat and reaction heat are detd., and the Joule heat, reaction heat as well as total heat generation rate is detailed and analyzed considering the influence of temp., aging, SOC, and current.  In order to validate the accuracy of heat generation rate, a lumped battery heat transfer model is applied to calc. the temp. variation, and the estd. temp. variation shows good correspondence with exptl. results under different currents and aging conditions.  Due to its simplicity, the temp. variation estn. method is suitable for real time applications.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGq-PWrhs00EG7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lig-kWg5kcW2g"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXhs1SjtL4%253D&amp;md5=efad08bcc53e18045f914a5cbe45d399</span></div></div></div></div></li></ol></div><script type="text/javascript" nonce="90f6e33bfd1a775c-LHR">window.refViewer={'ref1':['cit1'],'ref2':['cit2'],'ref3':['cit3'],'ref4':['cit4'],'ref5':['cit5'],'ref6':['cit6'],'ref7':['cit7'],'ref8':['cit8'],'ref9':['cit9'],'ref10':['cit10'],'ref11':['cit11'],'ref12':['cit12'],'ref13':['cit13'],'ref14':['cit14'],'ref15':['cit15'],'ref16':['cit16'],'ref17':['cit17'],'ref18':['cit18'],'ref19':['cit19'],'ref20':['cit20'],'ref21':['cit21'],'ref22':['cit22'],'ref23':['cit23'],'ref24':['cit24'],'ref25':['cit25'],'ref26':['cit26'],'ref27':['cit27'],'ref28':['cit28'],'ref29':['cit29'],'ref30':['cit30'],'ref31':['cit31'],'ref32':['cit32'],'ref33':['cit33'],'ref34':['cit34'],'ref35':['cit35'],'ref36':['cit36'],'ref37':['cit37'],'ref38':['cit38'],'ref39':['cit39'],'ref40':['cit40'],'ref41':['cit41'],'ref42':['cit42'],'ref43':['cit43'],'ref44':['cit44']}</script><div class="articleCitedByDropzone" data-pb-dropzone="articleCitedByDropzone"><div class="cited-by"><div class="article_content-header cited-content_header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div tabindex="0" class="article_content-title"><h2 id="citeThis">Cited By</h2><div class="article__copy"> <button class="article__copy__btn"><i aria-hidden="true" class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div></div></div><div class="cited-by__content"><div class="sciteMetricsDropzone">

                        rightTab-cas_cit1R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">1</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">α-Na2Ni2Fe(PO4)3: a dual positive/negative electrode material for sodium ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Essehli, R.; Belharouak, I.; Ben Yahia, H.; Chamoun, R.; Orayech, B.; El Bali, B.; Bouziane, K.; Zhou, X. L.; Zhou, Z.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Dalton Transactions</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">44</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">10</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">4526-4532</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">DTARAF</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1477-9226</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A new orthophosphate α-Na2Ni2Fe(PO4)3 was synthesized using a solid state reaction route, and its crystal structure was detd. from powder x-ray diffraction data.  The phys. properties of α-Na2Ni2Fe(PO4)3 were studied by magnetic and electrochem. measurements and by Moessbauer and Raman spectroscopy.  α-Na2Ni2Fe(PO4)3 crystallizes according to a stuffed α-CrPO4-type structure with the space group Imma and the cell parameters a = 10.42821(12), b = 13.19862(15), c = 6.47634(8) Å, and Z = 4.  The structure consists of a three-dimensional framework of octahedra and tetrahedra sharing corners and/or edges with channels along [100] and [010], in which the sodium atoms are located.  The 57Fe Moessbauer spectrum indicates that the Fe3+ cation is distributed over two crystallog. sites implying the presence of a Ni2+/Fe3+ statistical disorder.  Magnetic susceptibility follows the Curie-Weiss behavior above 100 K with θ = -114.3 K indicating the occurrence of predominant antiferromagnetic interactions.  Electrochem. tests indicate that during the first discharge to 1 V vs. Na+/Na in a sodium cell, one Na+ ion could be inserted into the α-Na2Ni2Fe(PO4)3 structure.  This has led to the formation of a new phase Na3Ni2Fe(PO4)3 which was found to be promising as a cathode material for sodium batteries.  When α-Na2Ni2Fe(PO4)3 is further discharged to 0.03 V, it delivers a capacity of 960 mA-h/g.  This corresponds to the intercalation of more than seven sodium atoms per formula unit which is an indication of a conversion-type behavior with the formation of metallic Fe and Ni.  When cycled in the voltage range 0.03-3 V vs. Na+/Na, at 20°, under the current rates of 50, 100, 200, and 400 mA/g, reversible capacities of 238, 196, 153, and 115 mA-h/g, resp., were obtained.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpw21ByM-sln7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0libdSaasdwvSg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhsVGiurY%253D&amp;md5=b941c2c9975f775eb2a129304216a4ad</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref2"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref2" class="rightTabRefNumLink">2</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit2" data-doi="10.1039/c5dt00971e"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Essehli, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Belharouak, I.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ben Yahia, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Maher, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Abouimrane, A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Orayech, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Calder, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, X.                         rightTab-cas_cit2R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">2</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Alluaudite Na2Co2Fe(PO4)3 as an electroactive material for sodium ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Essehli, R.; Belharouak, I.; Ben Yahia, H.; Maher, K.; Abouimrane, A.; Orayech, B.; Calder, S.; Zhou, X. L.; Zhou, Z.; Sun, Y-K.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Dalton Transactions</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">44</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">17</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">7881-7886</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The electroactive orthophosphate Na2Co2Fe(PO4)3 was synthesized using a solid state reaction.  Its crystal structure was solved using the combination of powder X-ray- and neutron-diffraction data.  This material crystallizes according to the alluaudite structure (S.G. C2/c).  The structure consists of edge sharing [MO6] octahedra (M = Fe, Co) resulting in chains parallel to [-101].  These chains are linked together via the [PO4] tetrahedra to form two distinct tunnels in which sodium cations are located.  The electrochem. properties of Na2Co2Fe(PO4)3 were evaluated by galvanostatic charge-discharge cycling.  During the first discharge to 0.03 V, Na2Co2Fe(PO4)3 delivers a specific capacity of 604 mA h g-1.  This capacity is equiv. to the reaction of &gt;7 sodium ions per formula unit.  Hence, this is a strong indication of a conversion-type reaction with the formation of metallic Fe and Co.  The subsequent charge and discharge involved the reaction of fewer Na ions as expected for a conversion reaction.  When discharged to 0.9 V, the material intercalated only one Na+-ion leading to the formation of a new phase Na3Co2Fe(PO4)3.  This phase could then be cycled reversibly with an av. voltage of 3.6 V vs. Na+/Na and a capacity of 110 mA h g-1.  This result is in good agreement with the theor. capacity expected from the extn./insertion of two sodium atoms in Na3Co2Fe(PO4)3.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqUKJ4AKPdoU7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljaEEBREEJxMw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXkvFGitL8%253D&amp;md5=f67235f5f9a8c7889e4874a1081c9f10</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref3"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref3" class="rightTabRefNumLink">3</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit3" data-doi="10.1016/j.jpowsour.2016.05.125"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Essehli, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ben Yahia, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Maher, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sougrati, M.                         rightTab-cas_cit3R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">3</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Unveiling the sodium intercalation properties in Na1.86.box.0.14Fe3(PO4)3</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Essehli, R.; Ben Yahia, H.; Maher, K.; Sougrati, M. T.; Abouimrane, A.; Park, J.-B.; Sun, Y.-K.; Al-Maadeed, M. A.; Belharouak, I.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Power Sources</span>

    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">324</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The new compd. Na1.86.box.0.14Fe3(PO4)3 was successfully synthesized via hydrothermal synthesis and its crystal structure was detd. using powder X-ray diffraction data.  Na1.86Fe3(PO4)3 was also characterized by operando XRD and Mossbauer spectroscopy, cyclic voltammetry, and galvanostatic cycling.  Na1.86Fe3(PO4)3 crystallizes with the alluaudite-type structure with the eight coordinated Na1 and Na2 sodium atoms located within the channels.  The combination of the Rietveld- and Mossbauer-analyses confirms that the sodium vacancies in the Na1 site are linked to a partial oxidn. of Fe2+ during synthesis.  The electrochem. tests indicated that Na1.86Fe3(PO4)3 is a 3 V sodium intercalating cathode.  At the current densities of 5, 10, and 20 mA g-1, the material delivers the specific capacities of 109, 97, and 80 mA h g-1, resp.  After 100 charge and discharge cycles, Na1.86Fe3(PO4)3 exhibited good sodium removal and uptake behavior although no optimizations of particle size, morphol., and carbon coating were performed.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGp2_7m-7w4JJrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljaEEBREEJxMw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XhtVSrsLnE&amp;md5=6aa18185f2d1665e528b4e011e37e65f</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref4"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref4" class="rightTabRefNumLink">4</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit4" data-doi="10.1016/j.jpowsour.2019.04.080"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kumar, P. Acta</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2018</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>292</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">98</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">106</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1016/j.electacta.2018.09.111</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit5R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">5</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Sodium intercalation/de-intercalation mechanism in Na4MnV(PO4)3 cathode materials</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Nisar, Umair; Shakoor, R. A.; Essehli, Rachid; Amin, Ruhul; Orayech, Brahim; Ahmad, Zubair; Kumar, P. Ramesh; Kahraman, Ramazan; Al-Qaradawi, Siham; Soliman, Ahmed</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Electrochimica Acta</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">292</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">98-106</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ELCAAV</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0013-4686</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Na4MnV(PO4)3 is a Na ion conducting material with a NASICON type crystal structure.  This phase is not much known as an electrode material.  The present work focuses on the Na ion intercalation/de-intercalation mechanism and charge/discharge behavior of the material.  The Na4MnV(PO4)3 was synthesized through a sol-gel process and characterized by XRD, SEM, and XPS.  The structural anal. confirms the formation of a phase pure cryst. material with nanometric particle size which adopts a trigonal crystal structure.  Galvanostatic intermittent titrn. technique (GITT) measurements indicate that Na4MnV(PO4)3 is electrochem. active having slanting voltage plateaus.  Ex-situ and In-situ XRD anal., as a function of Na concn., indicate that the intercalation/de-intercalation of Na is assocd. with a single-phase reaction rather than a biphasic reaction when cycled between 1.5 and 4.5 V.  The electrochem. measurements on composite electrodes, Na4MnV(PO4)3/CNTS (1 and 3%), show promising charge/discharge capacity (∼140 mAh/g), good cyclability (100% capacity retention after 40 cycles) and reasonable rate capability.  The cyclic voltammetry (CV) and XPS analyses indicate that the main contributions towards the activity of Na4MnV(PO4)3 can be attributed to the active of Mn2+/Mn3+ and V3+/V4+ redox couple with partial activity of V4+/V5+.  The obtained results suggest that Na4MnV(PO4)3 is a promising electrode material which can be achieved better rate performance with long cycling stability and battery performance through engineering of the particle morphol. and microstructure.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrU5lBfWFEHErVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljaEEBREEJxMw"> &gt;&gt;         </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries operating at ambient temp. hold great promise for use in grid energy storage owing to their significant cost advantages.  However, challenges remain in the development of suitable electrode materials to enable long lifespan and high rate capability.  Here we report a sodium super-ionic conductor structured electrode, sodium vanadium titanium phosphate, which delivers a high specific capacity of 147 mA h g-1 at a rate of 0.1 C and excellent capacity retentions at high rates.  A sym. sodium-ion full cell demonstrates a superior rate capability with a specific capacity of about 49 mA h g-1 at 20 C rate and ultralong lifetime over 10,000 cycles.  Furthermore, in situ synchrotron diffraction and X-ray absorption spectroscopy measurement are carried out to unravel the underlying sodium storage mechanism and charge compensation behavior.  Our results suggest the potential application of sym. batteries for electrochem. energy storage given the superior rate capability and long cycle life.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGryc79LGjyUJrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljaEEBREEJxMw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXhtVyqtrjP&amp;md5=aa5ff0b3b61b3100627a82e64ed46ef4</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref7"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref7" class="rightTabRefNumLink">7</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit7" data-doi="10.1021/acs.nanolett.6b05174"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cohn, A.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) have been pursued as a more cost-effective and more sustainable alternative to lithium-ion batteries (LIBs), but these advantages come at the expense of energy d.  In this work, we demonstrate that the challenge of energy d. for sodium chemistries can be overcome through an anode-free architecture enabled by the use of a nanocarbon nucleation layer formed on Al current collectors.  Electrochem. studies show this configuration to provide highly stable and efficient plating and stripping of sodium metal over a range of currents up to 4 mA/cm2, sodium loading up to 12 mAh/cm2, and with long-term durability exceeding 1000 cycles at a current of 0.5 mA/cm2.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Here we report a room-temp. sodium metal battery, where the sodium initially stored in a Na3V2(PO4)3 cathode is plated, upon charging, onto an aluminum current collector coated with a thin nucleation layer.  To maximize the battery performance, conventional sodium-ion anode materials, including non-graphitized carbons and sodium-alloying metals, were evaluated as nucleation layers to facilitate stable electroplating of sodium metal.  Among several materials studied, carbon black and bismuth showed the highest sodium plating-stripping coulombic efficiencies in half-cell testing, averaging 99.9% and 99.85%, resp., over 50 cycles at 0.5 mA cm-2.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Tailoring materials into nanostructure offers unprecedented opportunities in the utilization of their functional properties.  High-purity Na7V4(P2O7)4(PO4) with 1D nanostructure is prepd. as a cathode material for rechargeable Na-ion batteries.  An efficient synthetic approach is developed by carefully controlling the crystal growth in the molten sodium phosphate.  Based on the XRD, XPS, TG, and morphol. characterization, a molten-salt assisted mechanism for nanoarchitecture formation is revealed.  The prepd. Na7V4(P2O7)4(PO4) nanorod has rectangle sides and preferential [001] growth orientation.  Galvanostatic intermittent titrn. technique evaluation indicates that the sodium de/intercalation of Na7V4(P2O7)4(PO4) nanorod involves V3+/V4+ redox reaction and Na5V3.5+4(P2O7)4(PO4) as intermediate phase, which results in two pairs of potential plateaus at the equil. potentials of 3.8713 V (V3+/V3.5+) and 3.8879 V (V3.5+/V4+), resp.  The unique nanoarchitecture of the phase-pure Na7V4(P2O7)4(PO4) facilitates its reversible sodium de/intercalation, which is beneficial to the high-rate capability and the cycling stability.  The Na7V4(P2O7)4(PO4) cathode delivers 80% of the capacity (obtained at C/20) at the 10 C rate and 95% of the initial capacity after 200 cycles.  Therefore, it is feasible to design and fabricate an advanced rechargeable sodium-ion battery by employment of 1D nanostructured Na7V4(P2O7)4(PO4) as the cathode material.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGo4Qd2_IQczjbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgR-6y0KLkKgw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXos1Wltrw%253D&amp;md5=8f8ecee270b2407608b9eef53772a252</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref16"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref16" class="rightTabRefNumLink">16</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit16" data-doi="10.1002/anie.201912964"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hua, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xiao, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cortie, D.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Herein, a 4.0 V class high-voltage cathode material is introduced with a newly recognized sodium superionic conductor (NASICON)-type structure with cubic symmetry (space group P213), Na3V(PO3)3N.  A N-doped graphene oxide-wrapped Na3V(PO3)3N composite is synthesized with a uniform carbon coating layer, which shows excellent rate performance and outstanding cycling stability.  Its air/water stability and all-climate performance were carefully investigated.  A near-zero vol. change (ca. 0.40%) was obsd. for the first time based on in situ synchrotron X-ray diffraction, and the in situ X-ray absorption spectra revealed the V3.2+/V4.2+ redox reaction with high reversibility. Cubic Na3V2O2(PO4)2F nanoparticles are homogeneously trapped between conductive RGO sheets during its growth and assembled into a compact sandwich structure, which allows the elec. insulating Na3V2O2(PO4)2F nanoparticles to be wired up to a current collector through the underlying graphene conducting layers.  As a sodium-insertion cathode material, the structure exhibits a high reversible capacity of 120 mA h g-1 at a discharge rate of C/20 with a capacity retention of 100.4 mA h g-1 at 1 C and an excellent cyclic retention of 91.4% after the 200th cycle at C/10.  These results highlight the importance of anchoring Na3V2O2(PO4)2F on a conducting scaffold for max. utilization of the electrochem. active Na3V2O2(PO4)2F particles in a high-performance sodium-ion battery.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrzsZdwrMOS8LVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgR-6y0KLkKgw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3sXhtFWksrnN&amp;md5=98ffee6f2978d31d4a85610af6c8157e</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref19"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref19" class="rightTabRefNumLink">19</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit19" data-doi="10.1016/j.jpowsour.2016.05.096"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kumar, P.         </div><div class="casAbstract">LiNi0.5Mn1.5O4 is a promising high-voltage cathode for Li-ion battery fast charging applications.  Aware of its electrochem. stability issues, the material's surface is modified with small amts. of zirconia (ZrO2) ranging from 0.5 to 2% using a scalable ball milling process.  The advantage of the coating was demonstrated in electrochem. measurements performed at room temp. and 55°, and in cells discharged under high-rate conditions up to 80C.  Of significance, the material coated with 1.0% ZrO2 was cycled at the 40C rate for over a thousand cycles and retains 86% of its initial capacity.  The material with 2.0% ZrO2 modification preserves 76% of its initial capacity when cycled at the 40C rate and 55°.  The coated materials showed excellent cycling stability when subjected to 6C (10-min) fast charging and C/3 discharging for 300 cycles.  Compared to the uncoated material, the interfacial resistance of the zirconia modified LiNi0.5Mn1.5O4 is much lower and does not significantly increase with increasing the coating amt.  However, the electrochem. performances are still partly limited by both interfacial resistance at the beginning of charge and electrolyte diffusivity, particularly under higher rate cycling conditions.  Overall, the strategy of ZrO2 surface modification applied to LiNi0.5Mn1.5O4 unveils the potential that the material could play in extreme fast charged elec. vehicles.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqCAsGTw-LlybVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgR-6y0KLkKgw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXht1ertrzE&amp;md5=432c74d64609b07d9358012eedfc99cf</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref22"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref22" class="rightTabRefNumLink">22</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit22" data-doi="10.1016/j.ensm.2019.04.010"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Nguyen, L.         </div><div class="casAbstract">The Na-V fluorophosphate family was actively studied recently, but few examples tackle chem. doping or the substitution of V.  This work presents Fe-doped compds. Na3V2-yO2-yFey(PO4)2F1+y (y ≤ 0.3) prepd. by hydrothermal synthesis with low Fe content.  The amt. of Fe in the structure is confirmed by x-ray and neutron powder diffraction, electronic paramagnetic resonance, magnetic susceptibility measurements, and solid-state NMR (ssNMR).  The degree of V substitution, together with the soly. limit for Fe in Na-V fluorophosphates, was calcd. by ssNMR and magnetic susceptibility measurements to be y = 0.3 based on the synthetic route used here.  The introduction of small amts. of Fe3+ to the structure leads to the redn. of a fraction of V4+ to V3+, and the voltage profiles do not change with the introduction of Fe to the structure.  In situ synchrotron x-ray diffraction demonstrates that the electrochem.-structural changes during charge and discharge are very similar to those obsd. in the V3+/V4+ mixed-valent Na3V2O1.6(PO4)2F1.4, which could be related to the existence of both Fe dopant and V3+ in the phase.  This work presents Na-V fluorophosphates derived from the substitution of V in Na3(VO)2(PO4)2F with a low amt. of a trivalent species such as Fe3+.  Doping leads to V3+/4+ mixed valence and affects the magnetic and spectroscopic properties that can be related to the electrochem. performance of these compds., avoiding the loss of specific capacity assocd. with Na3Fe2(PO4)2F3. The materials crystallize in the disordered I4/mmm crystal structure as evidenced with electron diffraction and Rietveld refinement from powder x-ray diffraction data (Na3V1.2Fe0.8O1.6(PO4)2F1.4: a 6.38666(9), c 10.6562(2) Å, R = 0.023, RP = 0.013).  A combination of EELS and 57Fe Mossbauer spectroscopy revealed that V is in the mixed 4+/5+ oxidn. state, whereas Fe is exclusively in the 3+ state, thus pointing to the V4+ → Fe3+/V5+ co-substitution.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Ambient temp. Na-ion batteries are alternatives to com. dominant Li-ion batteries for larger scale stationary applications.  To realize such a Na-ion battery, electrodes need to be developed, understood, and improved.  Here, Na3V2O2(PO4)2F is studied from the perspective of Na.  Reaction mechanisms for this cathode during battery function include the following: (a) a region comprising at least 3 phases with subtly varying Na compns. that transform via 2 2-phase reaction mechanisms, which appears at the lower potential plateau-like region during both charge and discharge; an extended solid soln. region for majority of the cycling process, including most of the higher potential plateau; and (b) a 2nd 2-phase region near the highest charge state during charge and between the 1st and 2nd plateau-like regions during discharge.         </div><div class="casAbstract">The large abundance of Na combined with the feasibility of Na-based insertion compds., such as Na3V2(PO4)2F3, makes the Na-ion battery an attractive technol. compared with Li-ion battery for a few applications.  Nonetheless, one identified limitation of the Na3V2(PO4)2F3/HC system is its poor long-term cycling performance at elevated temp., hence the sorely need to screen the proper electrolyte formulation.  Here, we report a thorough survey aiming to assess the pros and cons of cyclic vs. linear carbonates with respect to the performances of Na3V2(PO4)2F3/HC cells.  Through complementary in-situ UV and CV anal. techniques we reveal the formation of sol. species stemming from the partial decompn. of linear carbonates (DMC and EMC) in redn. into sol. products, hence stressing their failure to provide a stable solid electrolyte interphase (SEI) at the hard carbon electrode and by the same token accounting for the poor performance of the overall cell.  We discuss the decompn. reaction paths, and propose a shuttle mechanism to account for the cell deterioration.  Our results, which underscores the detrimental effects of linear carbonates in full Na-ion Na3V2(PO4)2F3/HC cells, should serve as an impetus to identify superior electrolyte formulation for increasing the high temp. robustness of this technol.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoHtxUKlOUd1bVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0li87JsShAmXwQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXhtVWltbrE&amp;md5=c2a2599dc83def3f1133c49154b7f596</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref32"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref32" class="rightTabRefNumLink">32</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit32" data-doi="10.1149/2.0831802jes"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yan, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Dugas, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tarascon, J.-M.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">The Na3V2(PO4)2F3/Carbon Na-Ion Battery: Its Performance Understanding as Deduced from Differential Voltage Analysis</span>. <i>J. The cells show excellent long-term cycling performance (capacity decay less than 0.020 mAh g-1 per cycle at 1C rate whatever the electrolytes), but suffer at 55°C from copious self-discharge stemming from either redn. or oxidization of electrolytes.  It is deduced, from monitoring side reactions rate as a function of temp., the activation energies of 34 and 29 kJ mol-1 for the parasitic reactions proceeding at the anode and cathode side, resp.  The anal. protocol can be widely implemented for the fundamental investigation of side reactions between electrode and electrolyte interface in Na-ion battery; a must for optimizing battery performances via the screening of various electrolyte formulations.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoCDJtlSRsdKLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0li87JsShAmXwQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXjtlKjtLg%253D&amp;md5=e7801e221390cdefc563e8380ba27db0</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref33"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref33" class="rightTabRefNumLink">33</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit33" data-doi="10.1016/j.ensm.2019.07.040"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Essehli, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ben Yahia, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Amin, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">El-Mellouhi, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Belharouak, I.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Selective sodium-ion diffusion channels in Na2-xFe3(PO4)3 positive electrode for Na-ion batteries</span>. <i>Energy Storage Mater.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2020</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>24</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">343</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">350</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

        </div><div class="casAbstract">The electrochem. properties of carbon and reduced graphene-coated Na4Ni3(PO4)2P2O7 materials have been evaluated as high-voltage pos. electrodes for sodium-ion batteries.  Na4Ni3(PO4)2P2O7 exhibits the highest Ni3+/Ni2+ redox potential of 4.8 V vs.  Na+/Na with a theor. capacity of 127 mAh g-1.  Here, we report on the synthesis and characterizations of Na4Ni3(PO4)2P2O7-reduced graphene oxide and Na4Ni3(PO4)2P2O7-carbon composites. Carbon-coated Na4Ni3(PO4)2P2O7 composite electrode delivers a stable discharge capacity of 51 mAh g-1 at 0.1 C rate for 40 cycles which corresponds to a reversible intercalation/de-intercalation of 1.3 sodium ions.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Cathode materials that operate at high voltages are required to realize the commercialization of high-energy-d. sodium-ion batteries.                         rightTab-cas_cit38R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">38</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">A High Power-High Energy Na3V2(PO4)2F3 Sodium Cathode: Investigation of Transport Parameters, Rational Design and Realization</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhu, Changbao; Wu, Chao; Chen, Chia-Chin; Kopold, Peter; van Aken, Peter A.; Maier, Joachim; Yu, Yan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemistry of Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">29</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">12</span>),

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium ion batteries are realistic and promising alternatives to lithium due to the abundance of Na and the similar intercalation chem. of Na when compared to the lithium counterpart.  Developing high-power and high-energy sodium batteries is still a significant challenge.  Na3V2(PO4)2F3 (NVPF) has been shown to combine excellent charge-discharge kinetics with a competitively high voltage.  However, the major issue is, as for the vast majority of electrode materials, the lack of distinct knowledge of fundamental transport parameters, on which an optimized strategy for developing a high-power and high-energy sodium cathode can be based.  This work aims at filling this gap.  We exptl. investigate the intrinsic ionic and electronic conductivities, as well as the chem. diffusion coeff. of sodium of Na3V2(PO4)2F3 by impedance and dc polarization.  On the basis of these results, we develop an optimized design.  As the electronic cond. is found to be much smaller than the ionic one, electronic wiring of the particles (by a graphene network) has higher priority than providing electrolyte contact.  This is important since the contact by graphene and electrolyte wetting is partly antagonistic, not so much because of interfacial tensions rather because of the introduced heterogeneities on the nanoscale (cf. Lotus effect).  We develop and apply a one-step cost-effective low temp. hydrothermal method without any postheat treatment for the fabrication of a nanoparticulate (∼30-50 nm) NVPF electrode, which provides sufficient porosity and in which every nanoparticle is connected to the graphene network.  In terms of rate capability, the performance of this electrode is excellent and at least belongs to the best Na storage performances reported for Na3V2(PO4)2F3 so far.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGojv-JE23Bt6LVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljwxF1MRzABmQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXos1alurg%253D&amp;md5=a1aee1a498a19ac1ba20d70532253a9c</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref39"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref39" class="rightTabRefNumLink">39</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit39" data-doi="10.1149/1.1387224"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kim, J.-S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Prakash, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Selman, J.
